Various Industries Jointly Telegraph a Request for the Postponement of the "Responsible Transportation Regulations"

Various trade associations in the city telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Railways yesterday regarding the "Regulations on Responsible Transportation by Railway Freight Cars," requesting that commercial representatives be convened to discuss the regulations before they are implemented. The original telegram stated: "To the Honorable Executive Yuan and Ministry of Railways in Nanjing: Since the promulgation of the 'Regulations on Responsible Transportation by Railway Freight Cars,' various businesses have learned of its contents. Upon detailed review, the so-called 'responsible transportation' is, in fact, nothing more than an attempt to increase freight rates by 10%, while at the same time adding 19 exceptions in Article 36, leaving plenty of room for escape in the event of an incident. To call this 'responsible' is the height of absurdity. Moreover, in addition to increasing freight rates by 10%, there are as many as 11 types of miscellaneous fees. It is still unknown whether merchants will receive compensation in the event of an incident, but they must first pay an additional 10% freight and 11 types of miscellaneous fees, creating a heavy burden. Where is the convenience for merchants? Furthermore, it has established priority shipping and most priority shipping categories, with increased freight rates ranging from 30% to 60%. The number of railway cars is limited. Once this precedent is set, those who pay ordinary freight rates will be subject to long-term delays due to a lack of vehicles, forcing them to pay extra for priority shipping. This strategy is cleverly devised, but it is the merchants who transport goods who suffer. Railway companies transporting goods on behalf of customers is a business activity that should be governed by the national civil law and conducted in a spirit of consultation with merchants. How can it wield its overwhelming power with a threatening tone? Yesterday, we read a telegram from the special party departments of the two railways regarding this matter, which contained a peculiar argument: anyone who discusses the 'Regulations on Responsible Transportation' is a 'traitorous merchant.' This kind of arrogance is no different from 'punishing those who whisper and exterminating those who slander.' The country is guiding people towards the realm of democracy, but there is this abnormal phenomenon, which is extremely disheartening and makes it difficult to remain silent. It is reasonable to telegram Your Honorable Yuan and Ministry to review this matter and, following the example of last year's National Commercial Transportation Conference, allow commercial representatives to be convened to jointly discuss the Transportation Regulations before setting a date for implementation, in order to avoid obstacles. We earnestly request your approval. From the Shanghai Sugar Industry, Color Printing Industry, Aircraft Industry, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry, Dried Goods Industry, Silk and Satin Industry, Rice Shops, Seafood and Grocery Industry, Jute Bag Industry, Brick and Tile Industry, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry, Department Stores, Knitting Industry, Coal Ash Factory Industry, Lime Distribution Industry, and North-South Goods Exchange Industry, and over 230 other trade associations, with deep respect."

Miscellaneous Grain Industry Opposes Responsible Transportation

If Implemented, Shipments Will be Temporarily Suspended

The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Trade Association convened an emergency meeting of eight trade groups yesterday afternoon. 140 to 150 people attended, and representatives from the Bean and Rice Industry and the Flour Industry were also present. The meeting was called to order at 3 PM by Chairman Gu Xinyi, who reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that the meeting was convened because the Railway Responsible Transportation was scheduled to be implemented on September 1st, and the implementation date had arrived. The association urgently discussed how to respond. Subsequently, Chen Ziyi, the representative of the Bean and Rice Industry, reported that the Ministry of Railways had convened relevant commercial organizations in the Bank Association to explain the reasons for increasing the transportation price of Responsible Transportation. Chen represented his industry to participate, and read the regulations for Responsible Transportation established by the railway in public. Then, the chairman said that the industry shipped the most grain along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, so it was urgent to discuss a response. After discussion, the committee decided that among the three points of the brief explanation of the implementation of responsible transportation published by the Ministry of Railways, the true picture of the survey was quoted as saying that the railway freight rates were very fair, but merchants felt painful because the transportation companies added 50% to 10% to the handling fee. In order to provide a reason for the additional 10% of the responsibility freight, the transportation company will defend themselves. The association will publish its views to the Ministry of Railways in various newspapers. At the same time, it will send letters to merchants in Pukou, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Changshu, and other locations, so that if the railway is implemented on September 1st, all incoming goods will be temporarily suspended. The goods are being converted into ships and sailing boats. The discussion was over, and it was already 7:00 PM.

Northeast Postal Workers Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

A Total of Ninety People, Fifteen Remain in Yantai Due to Illness

Scheduled to Report to the Head Office This Morning

One hundred and five Northeast postal workers, travelling from Tianjin on the Jardine Matheson & Co.'s ship "Fosheng" to Shanghai, arrived in Shanghai at 8:00 AM yesterday, due to the Fosheng encountering wind en route, causing a slower voyage. The Shanghai Bureau of the Postal Administration and the Postal Workers' Union both dispatched representatives in advance to greet them at the dock. However, when the group passed through Yantai, fifteen of them fell ill and went ashore to recuperate in Yantai. The details are as follows:

▲ Arrival in Shanghai: The postal workers all belonged to inland bureaus in the Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang postal districts, totaling one hundred and five. They were all low-ranking postal workers such as mail carriers and laborers. They entered the customs from the Northeast at the end of last month and had been滞留 in Tianjin for almost a month. It was not until the 24th of this month that they received a general order from the head office, assigning them to work in Shanghai and Hangzhou. The postal workers then boarded the Jardine Matheson & Co.'s ship "Fosheng" southward on the 25th.

▲ Part of the Group Remained in Yantai: Shortly after the Fosheng set sail, when the ship passed through Yantai, fifteen of the postal workers, including postal carriers Zhang Guoshun, Shan Yongtai, Gao Wanzhong, Yin Fulong, Sun Yunqing, Wang Gaosheng, Zhang Zifeng, Zhang Naihai, Zhang Nailing, and Li Yurui, had become unwell. Furthermore, having grown up in the north, they were unaccustomed to sea travel, which caused them to suffer from seasickness. They disembarked in Yantai and were sent to a hospital by the local post office for recuperation. Therefore, the number of postal workers who arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning was only ninety.

▲ Arrival in Shanghai: Those who went to the Waibaidu Bridge Huashun Wharf on Gongping Road to greet them yesterday morning included two secretaries from the head office, Deputy Postal Director Dai Baoxin from the Shanghai Bureau, Chen Shengyang, Lao Jiemin, Gao Zongrui from the Postal Workers' Union, Cao Chongye, and more than twenty others from the Postal Labor Union. They all went to the wharf at 6:00 AM yesterday to wait. After the postal workers disembarked, they all boarded the mail delivery vehicles waiting at the wharf and drove to the Jingwu Athletic Association in Fudeli, Yokohama Road, to rest. They are scheduled to report to the head office again this morning. Except for three who will be sent to the Hangzhou Bureau to serve, the remaining eighty-seven will all remain in the Shanghai Bureau for placement.

▲ Representatives' Talk: The Datong News Agency reporter went to the Athletic Association yesterday afternoon to interview Na Wenqing (Manchu), Dong Sien, Xu Dianshuang, and other representatives of the postal workers. According to them, they were greatly threatened and enticed by the police and border police (organized by the Japanese) of the puppet state in the Northeast to stay and serve in the puppet bureau. However, we always put the motherland first and would rather abandon our families and brave dangers to enter the customs, and we will never serve the puppet state. It is also understood that only seven of the postal workers brought their families, and the rest were mostly left outside the customs because the puppet state's checks were extremely strict.

Representative Zheng Speaks on the Reasons for Slow Sales of National Goods

I hope that everyone present will pay attention, correct, and improve these issues. Moreover, I feel that the following three points are obstacles to the promotion of national goods: (1) unequal treaties have not been abolished, (2) there are no Chinese-funded banks overseas, and (3) there are no Chinese ships sailing overseas. If these three points cannot be achieved, there is no hope for the development of national goods." Therefore, I was ordered to come to Shanghai to collect national goods samples for the competition. Then, representatives from various factories spoke one after another, offering many words of encouragement. At around 5:00 PM, everyone took a photo, had refreshments, and the meeting adjourned.

Nanjing Road Merchants and Citizens Express Their Views on the Sanyou Factory Dispute

The Shanghai Nanjing Road Business Association and the First District Branch of Citizens' Association submitted petitions yesterday to the Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Municipal Government Social Affairs Bureau and Municipal Party Headquarters in Shanghai regarding the Sanyou Industrial Society factory closure and labor unrest. They requested a swift and impartial resolution in accordance with the law to maintain national goods industry and seek social peace. The two petitions are recorded below:

▲ Petition to the Central Party Headquarters and National Government: Petition requesting the Shanghai Municipal Government or to send personnel to swiftly resolve the Sanyou Industrial Society factory closure dispute impartially and in accordance with the law. According to a letter from member Sanyou Industrial Society, which stated (The original letter is the same as the letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which was seen in the previous report on the Chamber of Commerce's letter to the Municipal Government, omitted here), and so on to the association. Based on this, the reason and facts that Sanyou Society is unable to resume operations at the Yinxianggang factory have been repeatedly reported to the Shanghai Party and government authorities, and have been verified by reputable accountants appointed by the Municipal Government. Therefore, in the spirit of ruling the country by law, the matter should be swiftly arbitrated impartially in accordance with current industrial and commercial regulations. Otherwise, if the workers are allowed to make arbitrary and illegal demands, the truth will be obscured. Not only will the entire labor and management of Sanyou Society inevitably perish together, which is detrimental to all, but it will also cause great panic and discourage those who are engaged in real industry, hindering the budding Chinese industry, which is worrying for the future. The association, as a group of citizens and merchants, has a clearer view and feels a sense of crisis, so it cannot remain silent. It respectfully submits this petition, earnestly requesting your government to swiftly instruct the Shanghai Municipal Government or send personnel to arbitrate impartially in accordance with the law, stop the workers' demands and actions outside the law, so as to maintain the industry and seek social peace, which would be a great favor. (The rest is omitted)

▲ Petition to the Municipal Party and Government Agencies: Petition requesting impartial arbitration of the Sanyou Industrial Society factory closure dispute in accordance with the law, and a swift determination of a resolution plan to maintain the endangered industry and cultivate the fundamental livelihood of the people. The Yinxianggang factory of Sanyou Society is experiencing a work stoppage, causing twists and turns, and the dispute is intensifying, so that it has been delayed for nearly two months without resolution. The association, as a group of fellow citizens and merchants, has a clearer view. After examining the reasons for the factory closure, it is found that the factory's buildings are simple, the equipment is inherently unsound, and it has been eroded for many years and is unusable. After the January 28th Incident this year, it was occupied by the Japanese army, causing the machinery, accessories, and utensils to be destroyed. In addition, the economic turnover is inflexible, and the sales of goods are sluggish. After checking the factory's actual situation, it is indeed unable to resume work and has no choice but to close the factory in pain, in order to overcome the difficulties and preserve the remnants, indirectly still to maintain the lives of the workers in employment. If we must follow the illegal demands of the workers at the Yinxianggang factory and force the factory to open, it will inevitably affect all operations and cause everyone to perish together, which will cause even greater panic. The problem of unemployment is a major problem for the entire country and society, and the government should plan and solve it as a whole. If we insist on arranging workers' positions and use force to demand the opening of the factory by impossible means, making it impossible for the factory to operate freely, it is not only not allowed by law, but also the country's credit will be lost. Unexpectedly, the workers of Sanyou Society have persistent prejudices and create complications, and the dispute is intensifying. If this continues for a long time, not only will both labor and management of Sanyou Society be harmed, but it will also discourage entrepreneurs, which is worrying for the future when it is just budding. It is heard that your department has scheduled arbitration and a resolution is expected, which is very gratifying. However, the association is deeply afraid that the workers will obscure the situation in various ways and make demands outside the law, so it dares to submit this petition. It earnestly requests your department to review the case files reported by Sanyou Society in the past, and in the spirit of ruling the country by law, strictly correct the workers and make them obey in accordance with the current industrial and commercial regulations. It also respectfully requests that when deciding on this case, a feasible resolution plan be carefully drafted, so as to preserve the entire business of Sanyou Society and ensure the lives of the majority of employed workers, which is to maintain industry and benefit the people's livelihood, which would be a great favor. New Hurricane Warning Signal Method Established by the Jianghai Customs

Effective September 1st

Black Ball During the Day, Red Light at Night

The Jianghai Customs established a signal method of hanging balls and lights in 1929 to warn of hurricanes. Gu Xingen, the acting director of the port administration, has changed to a new method to facilitate the inspection of warning signals by merchant ships. Starting from September 1st, the hurricane warning signals originally located at the Lujiazui flag station will be cancelled and relocated to three locations: the customs rooftop, the Lanlu flag station, and the flagpole on the water tower of the Pingan Shipyard. The regulations are: (1) When the weather is predicted to be severe, two black balls will be suspended, one above the other, during the day, and one red light will be hung at night; (2) When a strong wind or hurricane is predicted, two black balls will be suspended, one above the other, during the day, and two red lights will be hung in a straight line at night. At the same time, a warning cannon will be fired once each at the Lujiazui and Lanlu flag stations in Pudong. This signal is to supplement the report of the hurricane and wind signals by the Xujiahui Observatory's signal tower, in order to warn merchant ships in the port. The acting port director issued Notice No. 8 yesterday, notifying the shipping companies to check.

Jiangtian Collides with a Civilian Boat

Five Drowned...Two Children Rescued

Civilian Boat Without Lights...Collision During Crossing

A Yangtze River steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company collided with a civilian boat near Wuhu, causing the boat to sink and five deaths. The Maritime Administration has been notified yesterday. The details are as follows:

▲ Collision Circumstances: The Jiangtian steamer was loading important cargo in Nanjing to enter Anhui. At 4:25 AM on the 24th of this month, when the ship arrived two miles upstream of Digang near Wuhu, a civilian boat was carrying passengers and goods from Liujadu to Yaojiagou. The civilian boat did not have lights and attempted to cross the river in front of the Jiangtian steamer. In the darkness, the Jiangtian steamer saw it too late to retreat and struck the civilian boat, causing it to sink immediately into the river, and all the passengers fell into the water.

▲ Five Drowned: After the small civilian boat sank, the captain of the Jiangtian, Qin Youyu, learned of this and ordered the ship to stop immediately and sent the entire crew to rescue the people who fell into the water. As a result, the boat was already broken and sank without a trace. Only two children, aged seventeen and fifteen, claiming to be surnamed Zha, the civilian boat was owned by their father, their father had fallen into the water, and four other men and women, including Yang Laosan, were also drowned. The boat was transporting reed mats from Liujadu to Yaojiagou. Since the bodies of the drowned could not be salvaged, the Jiangtian steamer sailed to Liujadu.

▲ Two Children Rescued: The Jiangtian steamer sent the two rescued children to Liujadu and handed them over to Wharf Director Sha Jingqing, who sent the two children to their family. It was determined that the incident was caused by the civilian boat without lights and the rough waters causing the collision. Captain Qin requested He Guangge, who was on the boat, to be a witness and prepared a letter to the local Public Security Bureau to indicate the issue of responsibility.

▲ Reporting to the Maritime Bureau: The captain of the Jiangtian steamer telegraphed the details of the incident to Shanghai yesterday, stating that the accident was caused by the civilian boat without lights and the rough waters in the dark causing the collision. The sunken boat and the five bodies of the drowned have not yet been salvaged. The officers on duty at the time of the incident were Jiang Chen Xiliang and Second Mate Liu Jianxing. Upon receiving the report, the head office forwarded the case to the Maritime Administration with the captain's original letter attached. The procedure for handling the case is still undecided.

Ye Lishao Sues Xu Jiping for Bigamy and Fraud

The Son's Date of Birth

Causes Laughter Among the Audience

The Judge Hopes for a Reconciliation

To Avoid Creating Materials for Newspapers

A complicated and bizarre love triangle case involving one woman and two husbands was continued in the fourth courtroom of the First Special District Court yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, presided over by Judge Fu Lin. Ye Lishao filed a criminal suit against Xu Jiping (also known as Xu Zhongxi) for fraud, bigamy, and obtaining property by deception. Both parties arrived in court with their respective lawyers. Judge Fu first asked the names of the plaintiff and defendant, and then said to the defendant Xu Jiping, "The plaintiff accuses you of (1) bigamy and (2) fraud. We are now checking whether the witness, lawyer Yang Changchi, has arrived in court." Chinese Police Officer No. 2591 reported that he had been summoned to Yang's office on Route Lafayette in the French Concession, but Yang was not there, and his clerk signed on his behalf. Then, the lawyer for the plaintiff, Ye Lishao, stated, "The firm of lawyer Yang is still on Jiangxi Road in the British Concession. The divorce agreement between Xu and Ye was actually signed in that lawyer's office. Therefore, the court has jurisdiction over the portion of the lawsuit involving fraud." The defendant's lawyer then retorted, "Whether the divorce agreement was signed in Yang's office or Yang's residence should be determined by Yang's testimony in court." Judge Fu declared that a lawyer's professional duties should be based on their office in principle, just as a judge's duties are based on working in the yamen [government office]. Now that the defendant has arrived in court, the phrase "location" has been determined.

Should Proceed with the Trial: The defendant was then asked about his age, and he replied that he was 25 years old. The plaintiff's lawyer immediately stated that the defendant was actually 28 years old and demanded that the defendant state his age truthfully. At that time, Xu asked to summon Yang Changchi to testify, saying that he had indeed signed the agreement at Yang's house in the French Concession. Judge Fu then reinterpreted the legal provisions on jurisdiction, and he remained silent. He then continued to testify that he had married Ye Lishao on March 20, 1928, and the witnesses were Cai Yaozhong and Ye Tongshu. The judge then asked Ye about the time of the marriage. According to Ye, she married Xu on March 20, 1927, at the Cangzhou Hotel in Hangzhou.

After the Marriage, She Returned to Fengjing: Her native place, and lived together for a month, then accompanied Xu to her mother's house, where they lived for about a year. During this period, she went to Hankou to do business, and the defendant went to Shanghai from time to time. She only knew that he came to Shanghai to study, and at first did not know that he had developed a relationship with Hu Bingheng. Before she and Xu were married, she had a son in January 1927. Later, when she returned home from Hankou, the son was gone. Xu said that the son had died. When asked where the body was, he said that it had been cremated.

As for His Marriage to Hu: According to his confession in the civil court, he divorced her in 1926. The reason on the surface was that he disliked that her house was small and did not want to live together. Lawyer Yang repeatedly sent letters to negotiate, and then a divorce agreement was signed, giving her 1,000 yuan in alimony. In addition, he paid 200 yuan for Duan'er's upbringing. Now she knows that Duan'er was not born to her, so she is suing him for fraud, totaling 1,200 yuan. Duan'er was born on May 5, 1928.

When Xu Jiping Heard This: He stated that Duan'er was born on May 25, 1929, and that the plaintiff deliberately made a mistake in the date of marriage, so everything was wrong. The audience and the lawyers of both parties could not help but laugh. Judge Fu also felt that this case was of little value and instructed the lawyers of both parties to go outside and persuade the parties to reconcile, saying that otherwise, the endless litigation would only create materials for the newspapers and cause both to lose their reputations, which would be extremely pointless. His words were heartfelt, and many who heard them were moved. The court then continued to hear Xu Jiping's testimony. He said that he married Hu in 1926 and Ye in 1928. The latter was according to his parents' wishes, while the former was a free love. Judge Fu then instructed him, "When you married Ye, it was a time of absolute liberation for the women's movement. You were a young student, how could you still follow your parents' wishes?" Xu replied, "There is still a reason for this. Ye's mother and my mother were old friends. In 1925, Ye's mother asked my mother to marry me to her daughter. My mother agreed. In the spring of that year, I met Hu at a classmate's house. In the autumn, I met her again on the Shanghai-Hangzhou train. At that time, I was still studying in Jiaxing. We began to exchange letters. The following spring, Hu proposed to me, but I insisted on monogamy, and Hu also agreed. On March 28, Hu came to the South Station and invited me to a hotel, and then we got married." He also vehemently denied Ye's claim that Xu had a son before they were married. At this point, both lawyers stated that there were some issues in this case that needed to be resolved after the civil case between Xu and Hu was decided. Therefore, they unanimously requested a postponement. However, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that Xu Jiping did not have a fixed residence and demanded that he be ordered to post bail. After considering this, Judge Fu decided to entrust the defendant to his lawyer, who would vouch that he would appear in court next time when summoned. He then agreed to postpone the hearing and still earnestly advised them to go outside and reconcile.

Taxpayers' Association Opposes Telephone Rate Hike

Another Letter to the Municipal Council Hoping to See a Reply Soon

Changes to the General Regulations Must Be Translated into Chinese and Published

The Shanghai Concession Taxpayers' Association sent another letter to the Public Concession Municipal Council yesterday regarding the opposition to the telephone rate hike: We are writing to inform you that we have received a letter from the Shanghai Special District Telephone Users' Association, which states that the Shanghai Telephone Company, under the pretext of changing new machines, vaguely requested the Municipal Council's approval to increase prices and to retroactively calculate from March. This kind of behavior is only to seek its monopoly interests and does not consider the decline of commerce after the war and the exhaustion of the social economy. This kind of behavior clearly violates the spirit of public undertakings. Reading the newspaper again, it was learned that the general regulations have been changed in secret, without announcement, only instructing users to go and consult them, which seems to lack respect for the interests of users. Our association was established by user organizations to jointly seek the legal interests of users and promote public improvement. Various Unions Support the Civil Movement Committee's Telegram Regarding the Electric Power Issue

Regarding the dispute at the Sanyou Factory, after the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee issued a telegram regarding the electric power issue, requesting the municipal government to use extraordinary measures to force the factory to reopen, it has aroused repercussions from various domestic goods factories and the China General Confederation of Industry, who have telegraphed the central government one after another, requesting that the order be withdrawn. At the same time, various labor unions have expressed their support, requesting strict enforcement. The Shanghai General Labor Union also issued a public announcement yesterday regarding this matter, and the Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District also issued a declaration. Excerpts are recorded below:

▲General Labor Union's Announcement to All Sectors It is hoped that people from all walks of life will take note: The Sanyou Industrial Co., Ltd. General Factory stopped work after the January 28th Incident. After the war ended and Shanghai was stabilized, all the workers, feeling deeply the pain of prolonged work stoppage, repeatedly appealed to the factory to resume work as soon as possible to maintain their livelihoods, but they were not granted permission. After repeated mediation by party and government organs, the capitalists repeatedly refused to attend, causing delays, and ultimately resulting in the tragic event of some workers being forced to go on a hunger strike. However, the capitalists remained unmoved, their cruelty being truly outrageous. As a result, public sentiment was indignant and public opinion was in an uproar. The Central People's Movement Committee, seeing that the capitalists were so stubborn and cunning, willing to let the workers starve to death without showing pity, intending to create a social terror situation, in order to prevent unfortunate events from occurring and to save the dying workers, issued a telegram regarding the electric power issue, requesting the municipal government to use extraordinary measures to handle this extremely urgent event. If this continues to be delayed, it will cause major social disturbances. Apart from using revolutionary measures to seek a solution, what other methods are there? It is regrettable that this still failed to awaken the conscience of the factory and cause them to suddenly realize their error. Instead, they have united with various factories, ignoring reason and justice, talking endlessly about laws, and publishing large-scale advertisements in major newspapers, creating a major public relations campaign, which has aroused resentment between labor and capital throughout the city. The association feels deeply regretful about this. However, looking at the advertisement, it talks about the law constantly. It should be known that the law is inseparable from human sentiment. Therefore, we will now state the "human sentiment" in this dispute. It is found that when the Sanyou Factory was first established in the early years of the Republic of China, the capital was only six hundred yuan. Later, due to the good management of the capitalists and the hard work of the workers, production efficiency increased, and the products became increasingly refined, which were happily purchased and used by the Chinese people. The company's business was able to develop gradually, and the annual profit was in the tens of thousands. Therefore, the capital was expanded year by year. Today, the Sanyou Company has become the only domestic goods factory in our country. This is due to the blood and sweat of all the workers in the past, which has made no small contribution. Now, due to the impact of the war, both labor and capital have suffered losses. However, the capitalists have earned a substantial profit over the years. Even after the changes, they still live in tall buildings and eat delicious food, living a comfortable life, while the workers rely on their ten fingers for food and clothing. Once the factory is closed and there is no work, what will happen to their lives? During this long period of work stoppage, everything has been pawned. The pain they endure is difficult to describe. If the capitalists have a conscience, how should they show consideration and pity for the thousands of workers who have worked hard for many years? They should find ways to provide relief, but they have not made any inquiries. Even when they starve and beg, they are unmoved. Is this fair in terms of reason and justice? Moreover, although the factory suffered an incident this time, the losses were not significant. The Hangzhou factory has been greatly expanded, and the store on Nanjing Road is also operating as usual. It is difficult to justify the excuse of being unable to resume work. Furthermore, regarding this dispute, the workers initially demanded that all work be resumed, but now they have retreated to restoring part of the work and expressed their understanding of the capitalists' difficulties, and are willing to voluntarily reduce their wages to assist in the development of the capitalists' business, hoping that the dispute can be resolved peacefully as soon as possible. Their pursuit was ineffective, and they did not resort to violent destructive methods, but to passive hunger strikes, their sincerity and purity of action were rare in past labor disputes. However, the capitalists have always insisted on their own views, with no room for maneuver. Although various parties have persuaded them with reason, they have not sincerely accepted, resulting in the dispute being prolonged and unresolved. To whom does the responsibility lie? It is very clear. The facts are all there, and all sectors of society can see it. There is no need for the association to elaborate. However, it is our duty to not remain silent, so we dare to state the above in order to seek a fair judgment.

▲Declaration of the Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District The Cotton Weaving Industry Union of the Seventh District, in response to the declaration advertisement published by the China General Confederation of Industry, etc., opposing the Central Committee's telegram, issued a special declaration stating that the temporary suspension of work at the Sanyou General Factory was due to avoiding danger. Since it was not approved in accordance with the law at the time, it should be resumed as soon as possible. The workers' hunger strike to seek work is a most legitimate measure. We should express our sympathy from a humanitarian standpoint. The factory suffered very little loss during the Shanghai war, and has accumulated huge profits over the years. Moreover, the dismantling and transportation of the general factory's machinery to Hangzhou for expansion, completely disregards the livelihoods of the old workers. Therefore, the Central Party Department's People's Movement Guidance Committee's telegram is in line with the party's position. Now, the China General Confederation of Industry, etc., are citing the clauses of absolute private rights of business freedom, regardless of whether their reasons are sufficient, their trend of jointly suppressing labor is conceivable. If class struggle is unfortunately triggered, the responsibility will naturally lie with them. Our association has always maintained a spirit of cooperation to seek the development of industry and commerce. It is absolutely inappropriate to shake the stability of the entire society with the interests of one party or one class. If the country has a large amount of land, but farmers are not allowed to cultivate it, and it is left barren in order to raise its rent, should the party and government intervene at that time? I hope everyone can calmly seek the livelihood of the entire nation, and stop killing each other and creating opportunities for enemies to invade and deceive us. I wonder what the wise capitalists think?

Explanation Meeting on the Photographic Printing of the Song Dynasty Edition of the Buddhist Canon

The Shanghai Photographic Printing Society of the Song Dynasty Edition of the Buddhist Canon sent a letter to various libraries and Buddhist groups throughout the country yesterday, stating, "Respectfully informing you that the Song Dynasty Edition of the Buddhist Canon has long been treasured at home and abroad. However, what is generally seen in records is only scattered volumes and individual books, which already indicates its special value. If one seeks the complete collection, which is vast and consists of thousands of volumes, it is truly a rare occurrence nowadays. Since the discovery of the Song Dynasty edition of the Buddhist Canon in Xi'an, our association has spent considerable time and effort compiling and collecting it. Every difference in the printing block, every slight damage to a single word or stroke has been carefully corrected and completed. This edition was published during the reign of Emperor Lizong of the Song Dynasty and completed during the reign of Emperor Wuzong of the Yuan Dynasty. It was created by the Yan Sheng Yuan of Qisha in Pingjiang Prefecture, totaling 1,522 kinds of sutras, vinaya, and treatises, with more than 6,300 volumes. At that time, Pingjiang, which is now Wu County, visited ancient temples in Jianghuai extensively, and this scripture has long been lost. Only Shaanxi Province still has an isolated copy. Colleagues are worried about the devastation caused by the chaos of war and the difficulty of cultural protection. Therefore, we are implementing a plan to photographically print and circulate it. We have previously sent photography technicians to Xi'an to select and produce a large number of glass plates for taking pictures, transported them to Shanghai, and will soon start selling pre-orders. The initial edition is planned to print 500 copies. All the detailed measures will be published in the newspapers at that time. Our association first states the intention of actively publishing this edition, because this scripture is a finely printed edition of the Song Dynasty and a huge legacy in world culture, not just related to one country or one religion and time. Benevolent people should have a deep understanding of this. As for the beauty of the original block printing and the rarity of errors and deletions, there is no need to repeat them. It is truly a responsibility that the people should bear to contribute to preservation. Therefore, since we started this project, we have been extremely quick in compiling the scriptures, extremely careful in photographing the blocks, and extremely low in pricing. The Beijing Qing Dynasty edition requires 5,000 yuan per copy, but this is only about one-tenth of that. This is different from commercial profiteering. Shanghai newspapers have repeatedly recorded this. We believe that you are always enthusiastic about circulating the Dharma treasures and promoting culture. We respectfully ask for your full support in promoting and ordering them. We are extremely grateful. We send our best wishes for the autumn season."

Yuangmingyuan Road Will Pilot One-Way Traffic

Jiangxi Road Bridge Closed to Traffic for Ten Days

The Public Works Department has now decided to pilot one-way traffic from south to north on Yuangmingyuan Road (between Beijing Road and Suzhou Road) starting from September 5th, with a trial period of three months, from 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM daily, except for Sundays and holidays. After the trial, if it is not considered satisfactory, it may be changed to north to south and trialed for another three months. The implementation of this measure is due to the recent heavy traffic congestion on Yuangmingyuan Road, where vehicles often cannot pass each other and must reverse a certain distance to proceed. The parking of vehicles on the west side of the road is a customary right that has been passed down for ten years. If it is canceled, it will cause much inconvenience. In 1930, one-way traffic from south to north was trialed. The opinion of the police department is that this direction is more suitable than north to south, but it may also be worthwhile to give the latter a trial opportunity to prove its advantages. In addition, the Jiangxi Road Bridge will be closed to traffic for ten days starting from August 30th due to urgent repairs.

Record of the Interrogation of Kidnappers in the Qian Miaofu Case

Published in the Newspaper with One Yuan Counted as One Hundred Yuan

The Kidnappers Initially Demanded 100,000 Yuan

Qian Guanjin, a local resident of Huayuan Garden, No. 7, Lane 606, Poon Tse Chi Road, French Concession, had some real estate, which aroused the covetousness of bandits. At 8:20 PM on the 20th of last month, his seven-year-old son Miaofu was cooling off in front of the door when four kidnappers suddenly came and kidnapped Miaofu, hiding him in a small boat in Alan Village, Huazhong Township, and demanding a huge ransom for his release. The victim received ten letters from the kidnappers, ordering him to paste notes and publish advertisements to negotiate the ransom price, and arranging meeting places. The negotiation was not successful. On the 13th of this month, Jin Jiulin, special officer of the French Concession Police Department, and detectives Zhang Ziying, Li Yaolong, and Bao Tan Qin Youyu arrested the kidnappers Wei Youwen in Pingji Li Road, and then arrested his accomplices Wang Shaoqing and Xu Dashunzi (all from Jiangbei) in Hongkou Tao Peng Road, and rescued the hostage. Wei and the other three were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, Wang Gangxu, the chief of the criminal court, sat in the first criminal court for interrogation. Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, first stated the case, accusing them of kidnapping and extortion under Article 371 of the Criminal Code. Qin Youyu, the detective in charge, reported the process of solving the case, arresting the defendants, and rescuing the hostage. Then, the victim Qian Guanjin brought his son Miaofu to testify about the kidnapping, stating that after the child was kidnapped, he received letters from the kidnappers every other day, a total of ten letters. They first demanded 50,000 yuan, then reduced it to 30,000 yuan, instructing him to write a note stating the number of 300 yuan and leave it at the entrance of the Yuanshangli Lane, Tiandong Zilaihuo Street, counting one yuan as one hundred yuan, requiring 30,000 yuan. Later, they instructed me to publish an advertisement, still counting one yuan as one hundred yuan to negotiate the price. I first published an advertisement offering 5 yuan, as if agreeing to offer 500 yuan, and later increased it to 30 yuan, willing to offer 3,000 yuan, but it was still not negotiated. Finally, they asked me to go to Huasheng Road and Jiangwan Road to negotiate, instructing me to carry an umbrella with a white towel on it as a signal. Because I was timid, I did not go. Later, the police detective sent someone to negotiate on my behalf, but it was still not successful, etc. He also submitted the letters and newspapers as evidence. Wei Youwen testified that he was 32 years old, lived on Xie Xu Road, and worked as a vegetable seller. Yang San, who is at large, came up with the idea. He came to my house at 10:00 AM on July 4th to discuss it, instructing me to invite people. I went with Yang to Wang Shaoqing's place to explain the kidnapping, and Wang also went to Xu Dashunzi's place to discuss it, and asked him to invite people. It was decided to meet at the Jinshuitai Tea House on the 14th. When I went to see Yang, Wang, Xu, and those invited by Xu, Chen Caigao, Li Xiangyuan, Xu Xiaorzi, Chen Dajizi, Zhang Xiaokunzi, etc. were already there. They agreed to do it on the evening of the 20th. On the appointed day, I did not go to participate in the kidnapping because of something else, etc. Wang Shaoqing testified that he was 27 years old and worked as a rickshaw puller. The previous statement was the same as Wei's statement, but he stated that he did not go because he was sick. On the 21st, Xu Dashunzi told me that the child had been kidnapped and hidden on a boat in Fahua. After that, I did not know anything about the negotiation, etc. Xu Dashunzi testified that he was 17 years old. Yang San, who is at large, and Wei Youwen and Wang Shaoqing, who are in custody, came to my place and instructed me to invite people. I recommended Chen Caigao, and then Chen invited Zhang Xiaokunzi, Li Xiangyuan, Xu Xiaorzi, Chen Dajizi, etc., who are at large. At 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the 20th, they gathered at Jinshuitai. At 8:00 PM that night, they set off and arrived at the Qian's house. Chen Caigao and Zhang Xiaokunzi each held a handgun and led the others who were at large inside to kidnap the child. Xu Xiaorzi and I took a rickshaw and fled. I was watching the wind outside. Wei and Wang did not go at the time. The next morning, Chen Caigao told me that the child was placed on a boat in Fahua. I told Wang Shaoqing. Afterwards, Chen Caigao was the only one who advocated writing letters and negotiating prices. I did not know anything. On the morning of August 11th, Chen Caigao and Zhang Xiaokunzi asked me to go to Wang Shaoqing's place. It was said that at 11:00 AM that day, they contacted the victim at the corner of Huasheng Road and Jiangwan Road. Later, Chen gave me a showerhead pistol and Zhang Xiaokunzi also held a handgun and went to negotiate, but it did not work out and they dispersed. The court verified the confessions and ordered that the interrogation be continued at 9:00 AM on September 8th. The defendants were returned to custody.

Concubine Sues Wife and Aunt After Husband's Death

Demanding 30,000 Yuan in Alimony

Fang Wenxue, who lived at 252 Chongqing Road, worked at the Jianghai Customs and had a good monthly income. His wife, Ms. Wang, lived with her husband, but Fang took Chen Shaqin, a woman from Suzhou, as his concubine five years ago, and lived separately at No. 1, Weishan Lane, Kai Zier Road, French Concession. Ms. Chen is now 29 years old. Since living with Fang, she has had no children. In February of this year, Fang Wenxue died of illness. Chen Shaqin, believing that his wife Fang Wang and aunt Fang Zhu did not care for her, hired lawyer Cai Liucheng to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, requesting mediation. As a result of the failed mediation, she formally sued Ms. Wang and Ms. Zhu. The petition stated that the plaintiff married Fang Wenxue, the husband of the defendant Fang Wang, as a concubine five years ago, and they had a close relationship. She initially lived at No. 1, Weishan Lane, and later lived with her husband in the old house on Chongqing Road, meeting his aunt Fang Zhu and family members. Later, Fang unfortunately fell ill, and the plaintiff took care of his medicine and did her best. However, her husband eventually died in February of this year. The plaintiff, alone, lost her support and felt that the wife, Fang Wang, was violent and threatened to deal with her with crude means. The plaintiff was worried about her future life, so she had repeatedly discussed with her husband's family members, believing that her husband's family had hundreds of thousands of dollars. The plaintiff was a member of the defendant's family and was also in charge of Fang Wenxue's estate. Therefore, she should be given a considerable amount of property or cash. At that time, Ms. Fang Zhu and her husband's family members all expressed their acceptance, but said that they would continue to talk about it after the funeral. However, Ms. Fang Wang took advantage of the funeral to take away the plaintiff's savings passbook and government bonds, refusing to return them. She also repeatedly delayed the alimony matter. The plaintiff had no choice but to request mediation from your court, but it failed. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit, requesting that the defendants be jointly and severally liable to pay the plaintiff 30,000 yuan in alimony. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Hu opened the eighth civil court for trial. The defendants did not appear and hired lawyer Lu Dingkui as their agent. Chen Shaqin, the plaintiff, was asked to testify, explaining the past situation and submitting a list of the defendant's property and land that she had investigated, saying that there were 5,000 yuan in unified tax government bonds, which her husband bought and gave to her, and a passbook with 2,500 yuan, which was deposited in the Xiangji Western Bookstore on Sichuan Road opened by her husband's younger brother, which had now been taken away by Fang Wang. She added that her parents were dead and she had no relatives to rely on and her life was difficult. Therefore, she requested 30,000 yuan in alimony. Judge Li then asked Chen Shaqin why she did not live with the wife. Chen replied that the wife was fierce and she could not live with her. He asked how much she needed to spend each month. She replied that she needed more than 200 yuan, including 20 yuan for rent, 5 yuan for a maid, 60 yuan for vegetables and rice, and several hundred yuan for buying clothes each year. Judge Li calculated that this would only cost more than 100 yuan per month. Now she was asking for 30,000 yuan, which would yield 240 yuan in interest per month at 8%, which was more than half of her budget. Therefore, she could only ask for 15,000 yuan. At this point, the defendant's agent, lawyer Lu, stood up and stated that Fang Wenxue had a total of six brothers living together and had not separated their families. The eldest was Wenxue, and the third brother had already passed away. Although the land submitted by the plaintiff to the court did exist, most of it had been rented out to others. Therefore, her statement that the defendant had hundreds of thousands of dollars in family property was not true. Moreover, the land was inherited from their ancestors and the brothers had not separated their families, so it was not solely owned by Wenxue. Judge Li stated that Fang Wang had not arrived, so the case could not proceed. He ordered that Fang Wang be summoned to court for further interrogation on the morning of September 6th.

Lu Qingxiang's Concubine Sues for Abandonment, Hoping for Alimony

Lu Qingxiang, the owner of the Qianhe Coal Store in Old Church, Xinzha Road Bridge, is quite wealthy. In addition to his wife, he took Ms. Bao, a woman from Pinghu, as his concubine on August 20th of the Republic of China. At that time, she was still young and did not know what it was like to be a minor wife. It was not until after the marriage that she realized the truth. However, the mistake had already been made, and she was still favored by Lu and his parents, so they lived in peace without complaint. However, Lu liked women and felt that one wife and one concubine were still not enough to satisfy his desires. He took a second concubine, and from then on, he abandoned the old for the new, ridiculing and scolding Ms. Bao. He gradually disliked her. He moved the newly married Jiang to the store and neglected Ms. Bao. Occasionally, when he returned home, they would always quarrel. Recently, he even denied Jiang, saying that they were living together and could separate freely. Ms. Bao tasted the meaning of his words, realizing that he wanted to abandon her halfway. She was afraid that she would be abandoned and would be old (she is now 33 years old), and she wondered how she would support herself. Therefore, she hired lawyer Zhang Deqin to file a petition in the First Special District Court, stating the circumstances of her marriage to Lu as a concubine, and stating that all the evidence would be presented at the trial. Since the concubine was a member of the family, all living expenses should be borne by the defendant. This is stipulated by law. Now the defendant is abandoning the plaintiff, so the fault lies entirely with the defendant. In order to protect her livelihood, she had no choice but to ask the defendant to pay alimony, calculated from the age of 33 this year until the age of 60, based on living expenses of 16 yuan per month, totaling 28 years, requiring 5,000 yuan. It was investigated that the defendant owns a large family property of 200,000 yuan. The plaintiff, having been abandoned by him, only requests 5,000 yuan in alimony. In terms of all the defendant's property, this is only requesting one-fortieth of it as a capital to live on for the rest of her life. In terms of reason and justice, it is not harsh. In addition, the plaintiff had private savings of 500 yuan, which the defendant took away on the pretext of lending it to his friend, and has not returned the principal or interest to this day. Therefore, she requested a judgment to (1) allow the plaintiff to break away from the defendant, (2) repay the loan of 500 yuan and interest, (3) pay the plaintiff 5,000 yuan in alimony, and declare provisional execution, and (4) all litigation costs in this case should be borne by the defendant. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang opened a court session, summoned both parties to question the facts, and then the lawyers on both sides debated to the end. The official ordered them to wait for a scheduled judgment.

Cylinder Burst, Injuring Three People

Car Instantly Shattered

Lu Taochang, a native of Tongzhou, 44 years old, drove a car to the Jiaotong Rubber Company at No. 641 North Henan Road and Baoshan Road yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, asking them to repair the car tires. Before Lu could park the car and get out, the cylinder suddenly burst and the car body was instantly shattered. At the same time, Lu's back was severely injured and bleeding profusely. Xu Afang, a colleague of the Jiaotong Rubber Company, was caught in the explosion and also injured in the chest. Ms. Xu, the owner of the tea shop next door, was watching from inside the counter and was also injured in the head by the explosion, suffering the most serious injuries. After the accident, the injured were sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by the Huishi Police Department's No. 112 Chinese patrol car. However, Ms. Xu's injury was particularly dangerous, so she was transferred to Guangren Hospital, and her life could not be guaranteed.

Water Pipe Merchants Provide Convenience to Fire Brigades

Installation of Fire Hydrants Requires Prior Reporting

Many stores and residents in Shanghai have installed underground fire hydrants for fire prevention. However, they do not inform the fire brigade in advance, which leads to the fire brigade members going to the scene after hearing the alarm, choosing distant water sources over nearby ones, often missing the opportunity to extinguish the fire effectively. The Shanghai South Fire Brigade Association, recognizing this issue, has requested the Municipal Public Works Bureau to instruct water pipe merchants to report to the association before installing fire hydrants and obtain a stamped certificate for coordination. The bureau believes that the reason is justified and will discuss unified measures with the Public Security Bureau. The Public Security Bureau will require the water pipe merchants installing the fire hydrants to directly report to the fire brigade in the district where the installation is taking place, and the fire brigade will send personnel to provide guidance. The fire brigade in the district will then report the installation details to the Public Security Bureau for record-keeping. It is reported that the Public Security Bureau has already issued a notice to all fire brigades. The Public Works Bureau has also notified the Zhabei Waterworks Companies in Mainland China to inquire whether the water pipe merchants have reported to the fire brigade and obtained a certificate before installing fire hydrants, otherwise, the water supply will be temporarily suspended.

Diplomatic Discussion on Collecting Foreign Banknote Tax Jiang Liqi

The issuance of banknotes by foreign banks in China has a long history, almost following each bank itself to supply local markets. At that time, Chinese people did not know the meaning of economic invasion, and even less did they know that foreign banknotes would affect China's finance. After the Boxer Rebellion, the psychology of belittling foreigners changed to fearing and trusting foreigners. Foreign banks took advantage of this weakness and issued more banknotes. The late Qing Dynasty and before the end of the European War was the heyday of foreign banknotes. In Shanghai, hard currency was mostly based on British silver dollars, and soft currency was mostly foreign banknotes in circulation. Even in the inland, foreign banknotes were widely used. An independent country must have its own specific monetary system, and the issuance of banknotes must be specially permitted by the state, which should not be interfered with by foreigners. However, at that time, hard currency was imported, and soft currency was mostly issued by foreign banks. Those who did not know the situation almost suspected whether they were still in Chinese territory. After the European War, the power of foreign banks was clearly exposed. The bankruptcy and suspension of payment of Sino-French, Daosheng, and German-Chinese banks gave the Chinese people a deep impression. Taking advantage of this opportunity, Chinese banks spared no effort in maintaining the credit of banknotes. With the rise of national consciousness, foreign banknotes gradually decreased and were replaced by Chinese banks. Today, foreign banknotes are rarely seen in the market. According to an estimate by Westerner G.E. Read in the Financial and Commercial Report, at the end of 1931, the total amount of foreign banknotes in circulation in Shanghai was only 3.98 million yuan. Although the accuracy cannot be guaranteed, it is indeed very different from the heyday of that year.

The issuance of banknotes should be specially permitted by the state and must be limited to domestic banks. This is the same in all countries in the world. The reason is needless to say. However, because of China's weakness, when foreign banks set up branches in China, they did not register with the Chinese government to obtain licenses, and even less did they obtain special permission from the Chinese government to issue banknotes. The government has never inquired about the amount of issuance or the reserve situation. Therefore, according to legal principles and previous Sino-foreign treaties, the Chinese government has never recognized the issuance of banknotes by foreign banks from the beginning, and it can be banned or revoked at any time. For example, when the National Government was in Guangdong, it prohibited the use of Hong Kong dollars in the market, and violators were severely punished. Foreign banks had no recourse and could not resist with the claim of previous recognition. The momentum of Hong Kong dollars was severely weakened. This is what we should pay special attention to.

Now, newspapers have published that the government plans to levy a banknote issuance tax, with a tax rate of 2.5% of the guarantee reserve, equivalent to 1% of the issuance amount. Chinese commercial banks, unable to bear the burden, have requested a postponement of the levy and a reduction of the tax rate, and have also requested equal treatment with foreign banks. The government has also solemnly promised that if the tax is levied, there will be no discrimination between Chinese and foreign banks. This author, in his humble opinion, cannot help but express his views. Whether the banknote tax should be levied, whether it can be levied, and whether the tax rate is reasonable and fair are not what this article intends to discuss. What I want to discuss now is whether the issuance of banknotes by foreign banks should be banned. If a ban is impossible, should it be given an informal special permission? After the special permission, will the future ban plan be affected? After consulting previous Sino-foreign treaties and correspondence, except for the treaty between Outer Mongolia and Russia regarding bank issuance, the right of foreign banks to issue banknotes has never been recognized. People can understand this only because of the country's accumulated weakness and the failure to negotiate revocation. If we now levy taxes on banks such as the Banque Sino-Belge, is this not equivalent to increasing their legal basis and clearly declaring that foreign banknotes have obtained the government's de facto special permission? When the situation changes in the future, or after the abolition of taels and the change to yuan, and the number of banknotes increases, foreign banknotes will inevitably take the opportunity to increase their issuance. At that time, even if the government wants to ban them, they will use tax payment as evidence of special permission. This action today will provide them with a guarantee for illegal rights and will be equivalent to recognizing improper gains. There is no better plan to avoid this. Therefore, I believe that if the government wants to levy a banknote tax, it should take this opportunity to negotiate the revocation of foreign banknotes and recover the lost rights. If revocation is not possible, it should follow the example of Guangdong and strictly prohibit their use, and violators should be punished. This is the best policy. If that is difficult to achieve, then inspect their issuance content and strictly supervise them, limiting them to the current amount of issuance and prohibiting further increases. However, a higher banknote tax than that levied on domestic banks should be imposed, and the right to increase the tax rate at any time should be reserved to show differentiation. This is a medium policy. If neither of the above two can be implemented, then temporarily postpone the matter and wait for future negotiations. For the time being, absolutely do not allow any legal basis for them to make excuses. This is the worst policy, but it is still better than being greedy for small, immediate gains and incurring great disasters and mistakes in the future. The national crisis is deepening, and the country is riddled with problems. It is hoped that the authorities will consider carefully and avoid giving others handles to use against us. It is like the three northeastern provinces, although they cannot be recovered immediately, the treaty to cede land will never be signed until death. My humble opinion is as such, and I hope that wise people in the country will correct me.

Free Talk Two-One Branch Tan, Ten-Zhang Light Line to Catch Honey Fish Zhan Lu

Sitting in the waterside pavilion of the West Garden, leaning on the railing and sipping tea, watching the three or five swimming fish, living in a glass kingdom, (this is not Glass-via), traveling together; inside here is thoroughly clear, casting a copper coin, one could see the copper coin landing, and there would be no concealment. Fish society is very bright, human society is more ashamed.

The tea guests next to me were talking about fish; some were talking about the five-colored fish of Yuquan, some were talking about the carp of the Yellow River, not just longing for fish while standing by the pond, but actually discussing fish while standing by the pond; among them, one guest spoke about the honey carp in the Siming Mountains, relishing it with great interest, worth recording a bit.

(Mencius gave up fish for bear paw, but what he spoke of was ordinary fish; if he had tasted the honey carp in the Siming Mountains; he would definitely give up the bear paw for the fish.)

Entering the Siming Mountains from Guangxi, about twenty-odd miles, there is a Honey Cliff, standing thousands of feet tall, overlooking a deep stream, this is the most elegant place with wind and shadow. Above the Honey Cliff, there used to be an incomparably large beehive, gathering millions of bees, which can probably be considered a first-class country in the bee world. When the honey is ripe, it drips into the stream drop by drop, resembling a few showers of sweet rain. The stream fish that eat this sweet water undergo a process of assimilation, and if the fish is made into sashimi, it is also sweet and without any foul taste; not only is the meat sweet, but it is sweet into the heart and liver; it is also like lovers in a love letter, worthy of being called sweet heart and liver. This kind of fish is not easily obtained, its name is Honey Carp; adding the word "gu" below the word "honey" means it is not only sweet, but also rich in feminine beauty, this is truly a treasure among fish.

Fishing for honey carp requires a cumbersome procedure; the fish are easily startled, and at the slightest touch of the hook, they leap desperately, often escaping. Moreover, the water below the Honey Cliff is clear to the bottom; if the fisherman uses a thick line, the fish sees the shadow of the line and swims away leisurely; if a light line is used, it is feared that it will not be strong enough to control the fish. Therefore, a light line of more than ten zhang is taken and wound around a bamboo pole. Upon reaching the stream, the line is slowly released. As soon as the fish is hooked, it is allowed to leap, with the pole and line loosened like flying a kite. When the fish that swallowed the hook is tired from leaping, the fisherman slowly reels in the line and obtains a honey carp of unparalleled sweetness.

Those sitting there, upon hearing this, all felt a sweet taste under their tongues, with saliva welling up.

Broken Hong Zero Goose Sends to Soldiers Shi Zi

Yesterday I went to visit my friend Hu Rixin. Hu is in charge of general affairs at a certain school. Previously, during the Shanghai Battle, the school was located in the war zone. The students were scattered. Hu joined the ambulance team. He spent seven weeks in the trenches. Among the corpses of enemy soldiers, he found dozens of letters and a diary. He asked someone who knew Japanese to translate them. He showed them to me. I quickly chose one or two to record below. Bones by the Wuding River, people in dreams in deep boudoirs. The warlords are greedy for war. Widowed wives. Orphaned children. It has always been the same at home and abroad.

(1) To my dear husband. The second letter from Shanghai has been received. The Chinese soldiers are so barbaric and strong, it is truly beyond expectations. You were slightly injured and are staying in a military hospital. It can be said that God is protecting you. I hope that the Chinese soldiers will retreat soon and that the Imperial Army will occupy the Chinese streets before you recover from your injuries, so that you will not have to go through terrifying battles again and can return triumphantly. The news of Fujiwara's death has not yet been known to his wife. However, she has not received a letter for two weeks, so his wife is extremely anxious. Fortunately, the news here is that the Imperial Army has repeatedly won victories in Shanghai. This is the consolation for the wife of the soldier. Our store has been taken care of by Yoshida (probably a shop assistant) since you left, and he has also been conscripted into the army, so no one is taking care of it. In addition, business is sluggish and taxes have increased, so it is impossible to maintain it. It closed yesterday. We will plan to resume business when you return triumphantly. Now I am sending a set of velvet rope shirt and trousers by mail. I hope you will wear it to keep warm. Attached are photos of your wife and beloved child (probably a daughter). I hope you will take good care of yourself and win glory for the Empire. Wife Chiyo. Dated February 23.

(2) To my son Yukio. You have not sent a single word since you were conscripted to Shanghai. It makes me very depressed. According to a letter from the Ozaki Miyamazo family, your brother died in Jilin on January 19 while suppressing bandits after being conscripted to Manchuria. His glorious death is admirable. Your younger brother became disabled while suppressing bandits in Kando. Of the three sons I gave birth to, you are now the only one I can hope for. (I don't know whether this old woman hopes for this son to die in battle or to return alive. But in the end, all three sons sacrificed for the country. This old woman is also very pitiful). I have been dazed and restless recently. If you can return and report your victory early, it will comfort me greatly. After receiving this letter, you must reply immediately to comfort me. I wish you all the best. Mother's writing. February 25.

Commemorative Medals of the 19th Route Army Huan Hua

In the January 28 Battle, the 19th Route Army fought bravely against Japan to defend national dignity and ethnic survival. At that time, the people praised the army for truly being the vanguard of the people, vowing to kill the enemy and breaking the selfish habits of soldiers in the past. Many people generously contributed their money to help the army; even students, exhausting their savings from frugal living, and laborers and peddlers, giving all their hard-earned money, all provided military supplies. This spirit of cooperation between the army and the people is enough to glimpse the people's ardent patriotism and the army's deep popularity.

Now, the army believes that the glorious war history of more than 30 days in the past also relied on the support of the people. In order to repay their righteousness, they specially made several commemorative medals and distributed them to compatriots who had donated money. The medals are made of iron and black, symbolizing the price of iron and blood paid by the army and the people. The top of the medal is a horizontal plaque, only an inch long and a fraction wide, cast with the six characters [Commemoration of the January 28th Resistance against Japan in Shanghai]. Below is a precious star, engraved with the words [Respectfully presented by Jiang Guangding, Cai Tingkai, and Dai Ji in the spring of the 21st year of the Republic of China]. Starting from the 25th of this month, they will be distributed to those who present their donation receipts from the past.

I secretly speculate that the army's intention in giving medals is not just for ordinary rewards. First, it allows those who are determined to endure hardship and avenge their humiliation to look at the object every day and remember their hatred, sharpening their determination to destroy Wu. Second, during this extraordinary national crisis, the army's spirit of sacrifice is a model for the people to resist insults. Third, the three provinces were lost overnight, but Shanghai was fortunate enough not to be lost like Zhao. Defending the country against the enemy relies on the unity of the people. Those who wear the medals should know what to strive for. As for encouraging those who do not have medals to love their country and feel ashamed of their indifference, that is a secondary matter. We should cherish this medal, understand its deep meaning, and carry it forward, and not take it lightly.

Autumn Wind Blows Away the Foreign Money Yimeng Zhonglou

Lost Hat Can Be Returned, But People's Hearts Cannot Be Measured

Although this is a very small matter, it may reflect a dark side of society. The fact is this:

Yesterday, I went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to receive the commemorative medal presented by the 19th Route Army. When I passed the Tianhou Temple Bridge, a gust of wind suddenly blew my straw hat off the bridge. I rushed to the bridgehead and looked down. Fortunately, my hat landed on the bow of a large barge parked in the bridge arch and did not fall into the water. I was about to shout for someone to get the hat off the boat, but in the blink of an eye, my hat disappeared. I asked the people next to me, and they all said that the people on the barge had taken it. So I had no choice but to go down to the river myself and cross to the barge from a few small boats. There were four or five people on the boat. I asked them about my lost hat, but they all said in unison that they had not seen it. Two of them even said: [The hat has already fallen into the water.] At this time, I could only look at the river and sigh for my lost hat. Just as I was about to return to the shore, someone came up to me and volunteered to get the hat for me, but he wanted me to pay the price. This made me very suspicious: [Didn't the hat blow into the water? Are you going to get it from the Dragon King now?] But since he volunteered, I gave him two jiao. This person took the money and walked to the person who had just said that the hat had fallen into the water, mumbled for a while, and then my hat was taken out from under the deck. In the end, when the volunteer returned the hat to me, his condition was to pay another two jiao as a reward...

Although the lost hat was still put back on my head, I felt great pain in my heart. I was not heartbroken by the four jiao that was blown away by the autumn wind, but by the fact that people's hearts in society are so unpredictable!

Remembering Xiangzi Bridge in Chaozhou Han Fengsheng

Near Chaozhou, there is a stone bridge called Xiangzi. It spans the Han River, starting from the west of Zhupaimen and ending at Hanshan. The stones are more than ten feet long and two feet thick, laid flat on the dams. Three stones are arranged to form one crossing, about seven feet wide. There are twelve crossings in total, and boats can pass underneath. Now, half of it has collapsed. Legend has it that it was built by the banished immortal Han Xiangzi. Xiangzi was the nephew of Changli (Han Yu). He did not like to study but was good at magic. Changli was appointed as the governor of Chaozhou, and Xiangzi followed him. He often went into the mountains and rivers and did not return for several days. His uncle scolded him, but he did not listen. One night, there was a great storm. The riverbank seemed to be filled with shouts from ten thousand people. The whole city was struck by lightning. The young men who went to see what was happening fell to the ground when they stepped out of their houses. The next day, the bridge was completed. Xiangzi disappeared without a trace. This is one version. There is an iron ox at the head of the bridge, which is very large. Legend has it that there used to be two oxen, standing on the left and right sides. The one on the right often trampled on the rice and ate the wheat, causing the farmers great pain. They prayed to heaven, and the ox flew away. The one on the left was also deeply buried, with only its back exposed. This is the one that still exists today. Both versions are far-fetched and unbelievable. However, the construction is so strange that it could not have been done by human power. It is no wonder that heresy is rampant. I served in Chaozhou for four years. Every evening, I would take a boat to the bridge and look up at the huge stones, which were occupied by bees and ants. The jagged rocks were terrifying. Leaving the boat, I crossed the stone steps and climbed onto the bridge. Above the dam, the shade of the banyan trees covered the area. Hundreds of local people lived in the trees that they had carved out. Hanshan Academy was the place where Changli studied. In the Ming and Qing Dynasties, it was a local school. Now, it has been changed into a normal school. The sound of bells often came from the bridge, making people yearn for the past. Chaozhou produces citrus fruits that are the best in the country. During the winter and spring, people gather at the citrus market on Hanshan. Buyers cross the bridge to go there. Several sections of the bridge have been destroyed, and one must take a boat to reach it. Alas! Ancient relics are decaying and in danger, but no one discusses their restoration. Is it that the power of the people today is not as great as that of the people in the past? I have been a guest in Jiangnan for three years. This summer, I returned and visited the bridge with feelings. I am afraid that the bridge will be buried. Therefore, I wrote this record.

Nightly Sacrificial Offerings by Datong Music Society to Two Musicians (Part Two) Han

Abusing emotion, creating a love triangle, and making a big mistake. Bringing two beauties together to live in the same house. I am a commoner, just a humble scholar. My family has nothing, so how can I afford to build a golden house to store two beauties? Falsely claiming to be a golden husband, able to form a harmonious union. Alas, a clever woman finds it hard to cook without rice. My poor darling, willing to dream of sharing a bed. Sadly hating myself, not having yet received a doctoral degree. Mounting debts, baskets empty. Creditors knocking at the door, my poetic heart constantly breaking. The shadows of the two ladies, soon to be eating wind and drinking dew. Struggling in poverty, where can I turn for help? Thus, illness arises from poverty, and sorrow from extreme joy. The six senses are about to be cut off, seeking medicine in vain. Misfortune strikes twice, alas, illness has penetrated deep into the body. Thus, leaving the Huangpu, heading for Huangshan, hoping for the rain of Dharma and the merciful clouds, relying on them as protection against demons. But alas, the power of the Heavenly Venerable Buddha still cannot ward off the impermanence of death. Last month, newspapers reported that Ji Hong died of illness in a certain temple on Huangshan Mountain in Anhui Province. His situation after death was desolate beyond description. Alas, Ji Hong, is this his own fault? Or is this his fate? A mound of yellow earth, forever burying his earthly soul. A few points of green phosphorus, forever weeping for his homeless ghost. Who will sweep his grave in the years to come? Who will offer sacrifices on the winter solstice? Alas, like Ji Kang, unfortunately, Taiping has ended the lingering sound in the human world (referring to the song "The City is Full of Wind and Rain"). Yan Hui died young, and the second sage grieved over his short life. Alas, how sad! The grief over Ji Hong has not yet faded, and the bad news of Tianhua is pressing in again. Tianhua is a rising star from my hometown. His learning and artistry are both above Ji Hong. Moreover, he pays attention to phonology, intending to revive the Music Bureau, reviving the decline of vocal music for thousands of years. His ambition is almost unparalleled. Tianhua's father, named Baoshan, was my classmate in childhood and companion in examinations. His writing is not weak, but he lacks luck in examinations and remains a scholar all his life. Tianhua's brother, named Bannong, also named Xiashi, has been in Beihua for a long time, and his reputation is very high. A few days ago, someone told me that Tianhua died of a five-day illness in Beijing. I did not believe it. Until a few days ago, I saw the matter in the Free Talk section of the Shen Bao, and then I believed it was true. Alas, the talents of both sons are enough to pass on the mantle of music, and to serve as pillars of my art. The future is immeasurable. But I am old and have short hair, already in my twilight years. My rope is short and my well is deep, and I can no longer hope to see them soar. Therefore, since hearing of the deaths of the two sons, I have felt my mind spinning and my nerves in turmoil. I lament that this culture is about to die out. Who can I rely on? I sigh that sound education is in decline. When will it be revived? Even those with strong power are like this. What will the old and declining do? Alas, Ji Hong, of course, is no exception. But Tianhua, with his noble character, always cherished a heart of white jade, and strictly adhered to his principles, never falling from his soaring ambition. Even if he could not have a long life like Guoshi Gong, why would he not live as long as Zhong Qi? What is called heaven is unknowable, and the gods are truly difficult to understand. Alas, may your spirit find rest!
